  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_75fef47e-9537-4ba4-8926-869673f9f5f5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

From Ran<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, he's clueless. It seems a lot of everyone's problems would be solved if thef didn't act like asses to everyone else just to "show them." From Rand to Elayne to Mat to Nyneave. A bunch of arrogant asses, all.<br />That pronunciation threw me off as well. I think it's because it's breaking syllables in unexpected places: Cai-rhi-en<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793271617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11357147118786464217"><i>"The lions sing and the hills take flight. The moon by day, and the sun by night. Blind woman, deaf man, jackdaw fool. Let the Lord of Chaos rule."</i><br/><br/>There is no going back. The Wheel of Time is now officially one of my favourite series of all time. At times while reading I got this weird, amazing feeling that only two other works of fantasy have given me before. There was something this sixth book had that took me over the edge and far down the other side. Or more specifically, something this book</span>
  <span id="freeText11357147118786464217" style="display:none"><i>"The lions sing and the hills take flight. The moon by day, and the sun by night. Blind woman, deaf man, jackdaw fool. Let the Lord of Chaos rule."</i><br /><br />There is no going back. The Wheel of Time is now officially one of my favourite series of all time. At times while reading I got this weird, amazing feeling that only two other works of fantasy have given me before. There was something this sixth book had that took me over the edge and far down the other side. Or more specifically, something this book did not have.<br /><br />This series has in my eyes had two huge problems barring it from a place among the very best fantasy epics out there. First, that the plot development is so slow it sometimes feels like watching the grass grow. Second, that the protagonists are the most frustrating, stupid, stubborn, arrogant idiots you’ll ever find in any series. And thanks be to some miracle, that second issue seems to have evaporated into thin air. While reading this book I found myself loving Mat and Egwene, feeling positively indifferent towards most of the others, and actually starting to like even Rand himself.<br /><br />And when you have an absodamnlutely amazing series and take away its single biggest problem, you’re left with… well, an absodamnlutely amazing series. Slow plot development or no, without the horrible characters that sometimes made me want to throw these books in the closest wall, I am truly able to appreciate the epic work of a man whom I would now describe as the best fantasy writer and world-builder since Tolkien himself.<br /><br />This was not the best Wheel of Time book so far, but it deserves all the stars simply for turning me into an adoring fan. And sure… tons of political intrigue, Forsaken point-of-view chapters, a Whitecloak actually being bloody awesome, and a return to the eerily wonderful Shadar Logoth; it all did help.<br /><br />Damn, I love this.<br /><br /><b><i>Wheel of Time reviews</i>:</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271575" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Eye of the World</i>
</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271557" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Great Hunt</i>

  <i>The Dragon Reborn</i>
</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271584" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Shadow Rising</i>
</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271654" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Fires of Heaven</i>
</a><br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271617" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Lord of Chaos</i>
</a><br />#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271658" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>A Crown of Swords</i>
</a><br />#8 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271669" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_51024325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51024325" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51024325?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51024325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5907982636801614689">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>I could almost copy and paste my review for Fires of Heaven right here and it would be mostly suitable because Lord of Chaos is more of the same. This is another metropolitan-city-phonebook-sized novel with a potentially interesting story that is bogged down by its excruciatingly slow pace, regular insertions of backstory, constant descriptions of the garb of every major and minor character (garb which keeps getting smoothed, straightened, or otherwise adj</span>
  <span id="freeText5907982636801614689" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />I could almost copy and paste my review for Fires of Heaven right here and it would be mostly suitable because Lord of Chaos is more of the same. This is another metropolitan-city-phonebook-sized novel with a potentially interesting story that is bogged down by its excruciatingly slow pace, regular insertions of backstory, constant descriptions of the garb of every major and minor character (garb which keeps getting smoothed, straightened, or otherwise adjusted), and too many mentions of expanses of bosoms, spankings, sitting on knees, sniffing, snorting, and braid yanking. (I swear, if I have to read "good stout Two-Rivers woolens" one more time...)<br /><br />In Lord of Chaos some of the most interesting WOT characters are absent (e.g., Egeanin and Lan), some of the formerly interesting characters have become almost intolerable (e.g., Siuan and Aviendha), and some who should have grown up by now just won't (Nynaeve and Faile). At least we get to visit a new city -- Ebou Dar .... in which everyone looks and acts the same and all the women are looking for fights (with knives).<br /><br />The only really entertaining parts of Lord of Chaos were Lews Therin's mumblings in Rand's head -- I thought this was clever and amusing:<br /><br />"Where are all the dead?" Lews Therin whispered. "Why will they not be silent?"<br />Rand chuckled grimly. Surely that had to be a joke.<br /><br />There is a climax at the end of the book that truly changes the course of the story (and I hope will serve to pick up the pace in the next novel), but it took entirely too long to get there and involved a sudden change in some of the characters' normal behavior. Rand's got a horde of Aiel maidens and wise ones around him everywhere he goes and then they suddenly decide to take a coffee break when a group of Aes Sedai come to visit? Huh? Well, I was puzzled, but at least there was finally some action, even if the events around it seemed contrived.<br /><br />Robert Jordan is a smooth writer who's got an interesting story to tell (thus, three stars), but he dilutes its power by drawing it out. This book's plot should have been combined with the previous two books' plots and then 75% of the words should have been removed. (There was so much repetition that we probably wouldn't have missed anything!). Then, instead of three slow and repetitive novels, we'd have one great novel. Read more <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/jordanrobert.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan book reviews at <i>Fantasy literature<i>. </i></i></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5907982636801614689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14558377037680657523"><b>
  <u>I am done!!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/>That's it. I'm out. I will not be reading anymore of this series because it is so annoyingly repetitive. The story has not moved forward for three books and the chapters and monologues all feel the same. The paragraphs feel the same, the sentences feel the same. It's almost like Robert Jordan is more interested in hitting a massive word count rather than writing a good story. <br/><br/>I was still curious to see how the series ended so I googled it and read the spoilers. A solid ending, i</span>
  <span id="freeText14558377037680657523" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>I am done!!!!</u>
</b><br><br>That's it. I'm out. I will not be reading anymore of this series because it is so annoyingly repetitive. The story has not moved forward for three books and the chapters and monologues all feel the same. The paragraphs feel the same, the sentences feel the same. It's almost like Robert Jordan is more interested in hitting a massive word count rather than writing a good story. <br><br>I was still curious to see how the series ended so I googled it and read the spoilers. A solid ending, if a little a-typical. I don't feel like I needed to read it to see it. This way is much better because I can actually go off now and read a good book. With this I found myself skimming huge sections and skipping chapters in their entirety because they were so boring. A book should not make you feel this way. I want to enjoy what I'm reading, not feel like it is a massive soul destroying chore that I don't want to partake in. <br><br> <u>The Wheel of Time</u><br>1. Eye of the World- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002483199?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">An unoriginal five stars</a><br>2. The Great Hunt- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360033546" rel="nofollow noopener"> A reluctant three stars</a><br>3. The Dragon Reborn- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497881147" rel="nofollow noopener">A well-developed four stars</a><br>4. The Shadow Rising- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982182213?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A strong four stars</a><br>5. The Fires of Heaven- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391618242" rel="nofollow noopener">A slow two stars</a><br>6. Lords of Chaos- <b>I am done!!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1436177441p8/1205774.jpg" width="400" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_404373711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373711" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404373711?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8130608-lord-of-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=book-outlet">book-outlet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404373711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5399962058271451635"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/06/review-lord-of-chaos-by-robert-jordan.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>NOTICE:</b> this reread is in preparation for finally biting the bullet and reading book 14. That means I HAVE NOT read book 14 yet. Please be mindful of this in the comments, both for me and for others who may or may not have progressed past this point in the series. Thank you.<br/><br/>SO . . . I'm not gonna sugar-coat it, shit goes DOWN in this book.<br/><br/>There's the Morgase situation, which is one unfortunate event after another.<br/><br/>We've watched the Pattern rearrange itself for Rand, Mat, a</span>
  <span id="freeText5399962058271451635" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/06/review-lord-of-chaos-by-robert-jordan.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>NOTICE:</b> this reread is in preparation for finally biting the bullet and reading book 14. That means I HAVE NOT read book 14 yet. Please be mindful of this in the comments, both for me and for others who may or may not have progressed past this point in the series. Thank you.<br><br>SO . . . I'm not gonna sugar-coat it, shit goes DOWN in this book.<br><br>There's the Morgase situation, which is one unfortunate event after another.<br><br>We've watched the Pattern rearrange itself for Rand, Mat, and Perrin. To their benefit. This almost seems like the opposite. And FYI, if you don't already know, I have NOT read WoT #14 yet (that's the purpose behind this reread), so if there <i>is</i> a reason, and you know it, you had better keep it to yourself. *brandishes fists*<br><br>Misinformation, coincidence, pessimism, logic, you name it, and somehow it's a contributing factor to the mess that is Morgase-on-the-run.<br><br>Also, you can't throw a rock without hitting a Forsaken. This is the installment where you learn what "Bal'azamon" meant when he went on and on about having power over the dead.<br><br>I'm torn between just accepting how realistically petty and squabbling these Big Bads are amongst themselves, and being . . . disgusted. You want reasons for why these powerful weilders-of-the-One-Power joined the Dark Side? Nine times out of ten it boils down to jealousy. If not jealousy, then resentment over some perceived slight. The notable exception is a Mad Scientist-type who was forbidden from continuing his bizarre genetic engineering experiments, but even that could be attributed back to resentment (for not adequately appreciating his "genius"). <br><br>So yeah, there's a surplus of scheming and machinations happening.<br><br>And that is not limited to the Forsaken, no, it is NOT. The Aes Sedai on both sides are behaving abominably. <br><br>Salidar Aes Sedai: the "Little Tower" decides the best way to legitimize their claim is raise their own Amyrlin. And that's a good idea. It makes sense. BUT. Even with the Tower broken and Tarmon Gai'don on the horizon, they can't lay their own goals and ambitions down long enough to come to an agreement, so what do they do?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Twist Tower law into raising an Accepted that ALL factions believe they can manipulate to their own ends. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Despicable. <br><br>Tower Aes Sedai: a delegation of Sisters--<i>including Reds</i>--arrives in Cairhien under the guise of honoring the Dragon Reborn and negotiating some kind of mutually beneficial "arrangement" that ultimately hinges on Rand's agreement to go (and presumably <i>stay</i>) in Tar Valon. BUT. The second they arrive they begin preparations for his refusal, in which case the new plan is to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[transfer delegation leadership to a Red (whose sole purpose is to find men who can channel and destroy that ability), forcibly abduct Rand, beat him into submission on the way to Aes Sedai HQ, and bring someone he cares about along as well, for motivation purposes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>SERIOUSLY.<br><br>Oh, and Alanna--currently unaffiliated with either group of Aes Sedai--takes it upon herself to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[bond Rand as her Warder. And just in case you didn't pick up on it, "takes it upon herself" means SHE DID NOT ASK. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And while we're on the subject of Aes Sedai, poor judgement, and superiority complexes, let's talk about their hierarchy.<br><br>What's it based on? <br><br>Age? Experience? Education?<br><br>NOPE. It's based on STRENGTH in the Power. As in the arbitrary amount of the True Source a woman can safely handle. <br><br>True story.<br><br>As Egwene observes:<br><br><i>Sorilea would have been put out of the Tower without ever being tested for Accepted.</i><br><br>And Sorilea is by all accounts the most respected Wise One in the Aiel nation. SO. It's no surprise that after their dealings with the Salidar Aes Sedai (who are by <i>far</i> the lesser of evils), any intimidation they originally felt has been replaced by scorn.<br><br>Just as concerning is the "Black Tower," run by Mazrim Taim . . . All I'm going to say about him is that if you're suspicious . . . you should go with that.<br><br>As disheartening as ALL of that sounds, it's not all bad.<br><br>There's Olver, the nine-year-old Cairhien orphan adopted by the Band. His story is heart-breaking, but he is resilient. And with an army of indulgent "uncles" he's infinitely better off then he was among the refugees. <br><br>Sulin-in-livery is also pretty great. *snickers* As is Davram Bashere, and Loial's reaction to learning that his mother has--as he's always feared--come after him with a bride in tow.<br><br>So yeah, good stuff to help break-up all the awfulness, but overall, this is <i>not</i> a happy installment. Be prepared to watch Rand slip further and further behind his wall of stone. <br><br>How will the Wise Ones teach him to bend like a willow so he does not shatter? I do not know. But I'm going to find out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705725321" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World (Wheel of Time, #1) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373567" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt (Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351590687" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Reborn (Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373656" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Rising (Wheel of Time, #4) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373676" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fires of Heaven (Wheel of Time, #5) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373844" rel="nofollow noopener">A Crown of Swords (Wheel of Time, #7) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373921" rel="nofollow noopener">The Path of Daggers (Wheel of Time, #8) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>

<div id="review_1655585043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655585043" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655585043?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655585043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12775848202791722077">A new month a new Wheel of Time book with the fantasy fanatics of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a>. <br/><br/>This book is both engaging and infuriating. If I were to write 30 words or less that sum up my feelings about the series so far they would go something like this.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Never have I read a series that I like so much based mostly on worldbuilding, plot and cultures while disliking or struggling with most of the characters.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>The continuing fight against The Dark One or Lord of Chaos and his chosen is re</span>
  <span id="freeText12775848202791722077" style="display:none">A new month a new Wheel of Time book with the fantasy fanatics of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a>. <br /><br />This book is both engaging and infuriating. If I were to write 30 words or less that sum up my feelings about the series so far they would go something like this.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Never have I read a series that I like so much based mostly on worldbuilding, plot and cultures while disliking or struggling with most of the characters.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />The continuing fight against The Dark One or Lord of Chaos and his chosen is really well done. I love all the details of the different cultures and the histories of how they were shaped that way. I think some of the reveals that are doled out here and there are masterfully in how they are planned and played out. The surprises that come in ever book again and again surprise me like they are supposed to and yet I can see the hints along the way. <b>Overall the story and world building are great and yet the characters infuriate me 73.89% of the time.</b><br /><br />Let’s just hit on the female characters first. There were a few that started off really good in the first few books and I thought they had a ton of potential but in this book I only like Min, Avienda and the Maidens the rest of the women spend their time hiding, making ridiculous statements, infighting and a plethora of other eyerolling actions that just make me cringe. Nynaeve who I adored in the first few books spent the majority of this one either pulling her braid, avoiding facing ANYTHING or just saying ridiculous things. *sadface* I loved her and now she is just a shadow of what she could have been. The same goes for Elayne, Egwene and Faile for that matter.<br /><br />Rand has the worst friends ever. I think the only people truly on his side all the time are the Maidens. I get that they don’t understand and are not sure how to deal with a man who can channel but Perrin and Mat were his best friends growing up and knew him before he was The Dragon Reborn. You would at least think that they would throw a little trust his way. As is it almost seems like each is ready to bolt the first chance they get and neither seems to have much trust for him. Poor Rand he is really mostly alone.<br /><br />But let’s get to my favorite moments in this one.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>ღ Loial finding out his mother and Erith are searching for him. Since he needs a wife to take him into hand and get him settled.<br /><br />ღ - Perrin finally meeting his in laws and finding they are just as hard and manipulative as his wife can be. They were funny though and it might have been my favorite happier moment this book<br /><br />ღ - Min getting her shot at Rand. It is about time and I love the way she has decided to go about it.<br /><br />ღ - Avienda and Elayne meeting up again after the Avienda spent some time with Rand….Man you would think that guy was Casanova instead of a woolhead that has no clue what to do with women.<br /><br />ღ - The big battle at the end and why Perrin had to take the fight to them. It was intense the the buildup was supurb.<br /><br />ღ - Egwene getting pulled into a very handsome mans dreams about her and *cough* getting her groove on *cough*</i>
</blockquote><br />Honestly it is a good thing that the story is really good or else the stubbornness and obstinacy of characters would really deter from everything else. There is some set up for some things to go either really right (doubtfully) or horribly wrong (more likely) in the next book and I’m really looking forward to that.<br /><br />I was a little sad that we didn’t get to see Lan in this book except for a moment. The Warder was one of the characters that I really loved in the beginning but he is getting less and less page time and I almost forgot about him completely except Nynaeve is also wondering what has become of him. <br /><br />All and all these while long are pretty entertaining stories and I have really enjoyed taking on one book a month of this fantasy series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12775848202791722077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1703503459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703503459" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703503459?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8130608-lord-of-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=wheel-of-time">wheel-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703503459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14911442850923748741"><b>*** 5 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my Fantasy Addicts at BB&B! May the Wheel weave as the Wheel wills!!! </b><br/><br/>Amazing! More than amazing! Have I covered it all?... Yes, I have! I have run out of superlatives for this series and I do not care! The pacing of the story is very deceptively slow, but it builds on itself, fiber by fiber, and by the end of each book you find yourself holding your breath, barely able to take in air, because it is an energy outward transmutation of a million plot lines coming togethe</span>
  <span id="freeText14911442850923748741" style="display:none"><b>*** 5 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my Fantasy Addicts at BB&amp;B! May the Wheel weave as the Wheel wills!!! </b><br /><br />Amazing! More than amazing! Have I covered it all?... Yes, I have! I have run out of superlatives for this series and I do not care! The pacing of the story is very deceptively slow, but it builds on itself, fiber by fiber, and by the end of each book you find yourself holding your breath, barely able to take in air, because it is an energy outward transmutation of a million plot lines coming together and creating an explosion!!! And you would think there is nothing left to write about after this, but the series is barely getting to its middle... I am in Awe of Robert Jordan! How he weaves all those settings, cultures, characters, plot lines, and creates a world so real it is palpable, I can not even imagine! Little details, which seem negligible, characters you might have noticed mentioned in the first book showing up now or at times you least expect it, every pebble on the path to every following book is there with a purpose and you truly get the schizophrenic sense that you live in the Real World at the same time as you live in the world created by Robert Jordan... And despite the feeling of a split, you enjoy every moment of it and want more, and more, and more... <br /><br />Now, don't get me wrong, Robert Jordan's world is not perfect, nor are the people and other creatures inhabiting it. We still follow mostly our five youths of The Two Rivers with the added from the first book constant companions, and they realy need to go to school on "How to communicate with the people I am closest to!", because they ALL SUCK AT COMMUNICATION!!! If they only stopped feeling sorry for themselves and start looking more on the big picture, things would be movie perfect. But, as most of us, they get stuck on the chicks or dudes they like-like, who is jealous of whom, power struggles, showing or not showing favors, love, guilt, shame, and fear... They feel real, flesh and blood, and are lovable, hated, or as annoying as anyone in our everyday life... The annoying thing does prevail at times, but it does give character to the books:):):) <br /><br />As always, I will not get into the plots of the books, since it is both impossible and it would be so much more fun to find it on your own... I will say that it starts slow and ends with a sprint. I can not wait to see what happens in the next one, which I am about to start ASAP.<br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and may reading expend your world and help you fly!!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14911442850923748741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158969299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158969299" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158969299?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158969299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1075477276619250453">To review this book, I have to start by telling a little story about my history with this series, and more specifically with this book.<br/><br/>It was in the great year of ought 7 (2007) when I was first reading Lord of Chaos, the sixth book of The Wheel of Time. It was also the same year that Harry Potter was finishing up and sadly when the author himself, Robert Jordan, died of a rare disease. <br/><br/>I decided, not only did I want to make sure there was an ending (sorry, I know that was insensitive of me), bu</span>
  <span id="freeText1075477276619250453" style="display:none">To review this book, I have to start by telling a little story about my history with this series, and more specifically with this book.<br /><br />It was in the great year of ought 7 (2007) when I was first reading Lord of Chaos, the sixth book of The Wheel of Time. It was also the same year that Harry Potter was finishing up and sadly when the author himself, Robert Jordan, died of a rare disease. <br /><br />I decided, not only did I want to make sure there was an ending (sorry, I know that was insensitive of me), but I was really excited to catch up and finish the Harry Potter Series.<br /><br />So, 4 years ago or so (since it's early 2012) I stopped reading Lord of Chaos just about 260 pages in. For me, for the last 4 years, Nynaeve, Elayne, and Moghedien were in Salidar for that entire time. Rand was still waiting for Elayne to come back and reclaim the Lion Throne in Caemlyn. Mat hanging with the Red Hand Band (they're touring in a town near you) and Perrin in the Two Rivers (which still felt like he was there forever when I picked up again). And I can't really say things change all that much by the end of Lord of Chaos either, but I'll get to that in the spoiler below.<br /><br />When I picked it up again last year, it was great to be back. I didn't realize how much I missed this series. I started by rereading (well, listening on audio) books 1-5 and then jumping into this book this year.<br /><br />I have to say, Lord of Chaos is where you can really see the slow-down take place. I love this series as much as the next guy, but there's a definite slow-down that happens, especially when you have a 70 page prologue.<br /><br />Some <b>spoiler-ish</b> things I'd like to talk about follow, so you may want to have read the book first. Just a warning.<br /><br />I'll start with the ending. As epic as it is with the battle of Dumai's Wells, with the Aiel meeting Aiel meeting Aes Sedai meeting with Aes Sedai meeting with Mayeners meeting with asha'man meeting with..okay I'll stop there. Okay, awesome battle, I loved it, but it was extremely short. It was really only the last 30 pages or so. But the main part is that it really didn't do a whole lot to move the story forward like I thought the ending of the book would do. <br /><br />No Forsaken is killed like in all the others up to this point. Okay, it shows the power and threat that is the Asha'man as well as the Shaido who've been pretty worthless for a while now. Otherwise, it just resolves problems that were just introduced in this book and then adds more. Am I gonna have to make another Lost comparison?<br /><br />Next, what's the deal with the bowl that controls weather (that's not yet found)? I figured the way to solve the problem with the rising heat being due to the Dark One's influence was to...mmmm...defeat the Dark One. We don't need another random track to go down.<br /><br />End Spoiler Discussion<br /><br />So, if you read the spoiler, I really did enjoy this installment in The Wheel of Time, promise. If you didn't read the spoiler, I really did enjoy this installment in The Wheel of Time. Not my favorite in the series, but I really enjoyed all the intricacies and additions to the incredible world Jordan created.<br /><br />4.5/5 Stars<br /><br />Ps. This is a <a href="http://www.youtube.com/embed/xxhhnzHjggQ" rel="nofollow noopener">cool video </a>of the making of the new ebook cover. I don't recommend watching it until you've read the book though. It combines the artwork with passages from the audiobook read by Michael Kramer including some of the very last lines of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1075477276619250453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2512747720?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8130608-lord-of-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=br-with-ini">br-with-ini</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512747720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7645317887414805321">This was a slooooow book and took almost 50-55% to actually get started. So you can imagine how frustrated I was while reading this at snail's pace, kept thinking when will things start happening. And even after all my grumbling, this was a necessary book because here we see characters coming out of their shells. I will keep this review short. <br/><br/>About the boys - Rand just keep improving his game of politics. getting stronger at making people obey and follow him. He is so much different from the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7645317887414805321" style="display:none">This was a slooooow book and took almost 50-55% to actually get started. So you can imagine how frustrated I was while reading this at snail's pace, kept thinking when will things start happening. And even after all my grumbling, this was a necessary book because here we see characters coming out of their shells. I will keep this review short. <br /><br />About the boys - Rand just keep improving his game of politics. getting stronger at making people obey and follow him. He is so much different from the boy that we first met in Eye of the World. The best thing I like about him is that he's accepted what he is and knows what he has to do. Future of the world depends on him. There is no softness about him, even though he feel sad whenever someone sacrifice his or her life for him but there is no time to be sappy and cry. And he is excelling at this with each book. <br /><br />I was so happy that Perrin's back and I was thinking of all the ways in which he could help Rand but too bad that Perrin drowned himself in worry over his wife, Faile. <br /><br />Mat was so much fun. He made this book bearable for first half with his jokes and what would he do if any of the girl disobeyed him. Of course, girls proved to be a tougher opponents than he was expecting. <br /><br />About the girls - this book belongs to Egwene. So much power at her dispense and I am eager to see how she would use it or she would be just a puppet of other Aes Sedais. <br /><br />Nynaeve and Elyane should be best friends as they are together since book 4. Sadly they are not. I am disappointed in Nynaeve in this book. What happened to the fierce girl that I love? She was so meek here. <br /><br />Min and Aviendha, felt like secondary characters. I am not a fan of Aviendha, so am just happy that she was not here much. Min finally made her way back to Rand and it was good to see them together and Min always keep things interested with her prophecies.<br /><br />As usual I loved the final battle and the slow pace of the book was forgotten/forgiven. So much happened in the last few chapters that I was constantly on the edge. The way things ended here I am so eager to start A Crown of Swords. Hoping against hope that it would be better than this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7645317887414805321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_380943074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380943074" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380943074?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781429960533" href="/book/show/7861268-lord-of-chaos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380943074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6074896351880946288">This book contains much more different point of views than the first five; we even get to see the inner thoughts of some of the Forsaken. Each POV usually contributes to a different plot, subplot, or thread which makes a really complex overall story, so if you thought the one in the first five books was way too simple (I am kidding), this book really makes matters <b>much</b> more complex. This is also the point where the number of named characters became too great for all of them to be in the glossary</span>
  <span id="freeText6074896351880946288" style="display:none">This book contains much more different point of views than the first five; we even get to see the inner thoughts of some of the Forsaken. Each POV usually contributes to a different plot, subplot, or thread which makes a really complex overall story, so if you thought the one in the first five books was way too simple (I am kidding), this book really makes matters <b>much</b> more complex. This is also the point where the number of named characters became too great for all of them to be in the glossary at the end.<br /><br />As usual to avoid the spoilers I will give the analysis of the character development and my thoughts about them. Any mention of the plot at this time would be a spoiler.<br /><br />The Dragon Reborn himself is an interesting study about his true identity. Is he really reborn, reincarnated or his own person completely independent from Lews Therin? Do not expect an easy answer to this question.<br /><br />Rand spends most of his time jumping between Caemlin and Caerhien while trying to hold the throne of the first until Elaine comes back, but she is not a big hurry to do it; I will comment on her later.<br /><br />Perrin finally shows up, but I am sorry to say he is reduced from a person to a rug by Faile who firmly guides him. He has his brief moment of glory by the end of the book, but even then the scene is stolen by other characters.<br /><br />Mat is interesting, as usual. His plot line makes an interesting and unexpected turn by the middle of the book. The way he gets treated by Wonder Girls (Nynaeve, Elaine, and Egwene) is inexcusable. Rand uses him as well, but at least he realizes it and feels regret doing this; most of the time he really does not have a choice. The Wonder Girls (ab)use his without a second thought.<br /><br />Nynaeve at least has decency to avoid Mat most of the time. She also begins to shine as a healer who can hold on her own even compared to the great healers from the Age of Legends. She is directly responsible for one of the most emotional part of the book.<br /><br />Anybody with the last name Trankand should be shot with belfire - simple as that with Galad being one possible exception: his is not in this book. Morgaise betrayed her kingdom - yes, what she did was a betrayal regardless of what her motivations were. Elaine does not care about her kingdom much as well: she prefers Aes Sedai intrigues to going back to her throne which Rand has real troubles holding for her. Do not even let me start on Gawyn, he moved to bad guys' camp in my book and firmly rooted in there.<br /><br />The book is interesting and good enough to warrant easy 4 stars. The reason for 5 star rating? Two words: Dumai's Wells. This has got to be one of the most memorable battles in fantasy literature with even more exciting and interesting aftermath. This also happens to be the last book of the series which deserves five stars before the infamous slowdown; a must-read. <br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my BoolLikes one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gene.booklikes.com/post/753100/did-you-think-the-plot-of-the-previous-books-was-too-simple-this-one-complicates-things-by-tenfold">http://gene.booklikes.com/post/753100...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6074896351880946288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_837070084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837070084" />
    <a title="Olivier Delaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9854601-olivier-delaye"><img alt="Olivier Delaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582470792p2/9854601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/837070084?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivier Delaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivier Delaye" href="/user/show/9854601-olivier-delaye">Olivier Delaye</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7983006304808496455">THIS IS MEANT AS A LIGHT, NOT-TOO-SERIOUS BUT HOPEFULLY FUNNY REVIEW, SO PLEASE TAKE IT FOR WHAT IT IS. AND NOW, ON TO THE SLAUGHTER!!!<br/><br/>Nyneave tugged her braid as hard as she could bear it. Any harder and she would surely rip her scalp off. “How am I supposed to review this book?” she muttered, holding a copy of Robert Jordan’s Lord of Chaos in her left hand. Her right was busy pulling at her braid. “The author’s first three books were really good––well, if one turns a blind eye on the fact that</span>
  <span id="freeText7983006304808496455" style="display:none">THIS IS MEANT AS A LIGHT, NOT-TOO-SERIOUS BUT HOPEFULLY FUNNY REVIEW, SO PLEASE TAKE IT FOR WHAT IT IS. AND NOW, ON TO THE SLAUGHTER!!!<br /><br />Nyneave tugged her braid as hard as she could bear it. Any harder and she would surely rip her scalp off. “How am I supposed to review this book?” she muttered, holding a copy of Robert Jordan’s Lord of Chaos in her left hand. Her right was busy pulling at her braid. “The author’s first three books were really good––well, if one turns a blind eye on the fact that they are LOTR ripoffs, which, don’t get me wrong, is fine by me, just as long as the story is revisited in a captivating way and makes you turn the pages faster than it takes for my right hand to reach up and tug my braid; speaking of which…––but book 4 and 5 were pretty hard to slog through and I’m afraid the same can be said about book 6. The ending is pretty good, though. Quite unexpected, you might say. Ah, men!”<br /><br />Elayne listened to her friend, the faintest ghost of the beginning of a smile slightly spiced up by the undeniable tinge of mockery embodied in the ever so feeble and elusive yet very much there glint in her left eye which, much like her right eye, was the color of the sea and the sky when it is not yet noon although the eleventh hour of the day is well nigh passed and gone. “My dear sweet good friend Nyneave, what troubles you so, pray tell your dear sweet good friend Elayne?”<br /><br />Nyneave glared at Elayne, a pearly thread of saliva dangling from the left corner of her mouth whose full lips were the color of the sky when it is not yet dawn although dusk is long passed and gone. She had never been so angry in her life! Well, not since five minutes ago, anyway. “Are you deaf, woman? Woolheaded perhaps?” She gave her braid another tug, this time hard enough to make her scream in pain. It felt good, though. Indeed, it felt quite pleasurable. Like, pleasing. The opposite of unpleasant. Or that of disagreeable. You know, like, good. For the pain reminded her she was alive and had hair to tug at. And so she tugged at it one more time for good measure. “I just said out loud that I didn’t know what to make of book 6 in the Wheel of Time series. I warned you time and again not to listen to your iPod so often, woman. And what did her Highness do? You kept on listening to that woolheaded contraption of a thing and made yourself deaf. Ah, women!”<br /><br />Elayne chose not to answer to that ill-founded accusation. She put both her bejeweled hands palm up on her lap, smoothing backhandedly the delicate fabric of her dress which was made of a multitude of silk and damask and cotton and acrylic and elastane cloth leaves, each perfectly and masterfully and skillfully sewn together and each having its own particular hue which very often reminded the onlooker––or for that matter the bearer, for dresses were meant to be worn in this part of Randland and not only admired and wrote about for thousands and thousands and thousands of pages––of the color of an autumn sky when summer is definitely passed and gone but winter is not yet there and bides its time dozing patiently at the corner of November and December, and said, “I think you should know by now that the author––the Gods rest his soul––only wrote books 6 through 11 of his series because his editor, who also happened to be his wife, had thrown in the towel well before the Breaking of the World. So he basically wrote whatever he wanted for as many pages as he wanted, not giving a rat’s ass about moving the plot along or shutting it up about what this and that Aes Sedai is wearing in this and that scene. Image how fun it must have been for him! Quite a treat, really. Not so much for us readers, though… So here’s what you should do, sweet beautiful Nyneave: don’t bother reading book 6 through 11––I know I won’t; just Google the plot summaries (ah, ah, ah, the plot! That’s a good one!) and then move on to book 12 The Gathering Storm by Brandon Sanderson. Here, you can even use my iPod. That way you’ll have your hands free to do as much braid pulling as you want while listening to the audiobook. Aren’t I a great friend, sweet beautiful gorgeous Nyneave?”<br /><br />“Burn you, woman, burn you and your fancy gadgets to the hundred hells below!” In her rage, Nyneave went on tugging at her braid like a demented Quasimodo pulling at the bell rope of Notre-Dame on a wedding day. She tugged hard. Oh boy, did she. Really, really hard. A little too hard perhaps. For in the end she broke her cervical spine, leaving her paralyzed from the neck down.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7983006304808496455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_484735185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484735185" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484735185?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=acquired-in-2013">acquired-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=must-read-in-2015">must-read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484735185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9612278914636215135"><i>Was the whole world really burning up?</i><br/><br/>Thank goodness for the Wheel of Time <b>Wikia</b> page. At this point in the series I can’t really differentiate too clearly between books; everything is just blurring together. I suppose it would help if I read the books back to back, but that is not a realistic option. I honestly need a break between instalments. <br/><br/>That said, I do believe I enjoyed this book more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13895.The_Fires_of_Heaven__Wheel_of_Time___5_' title='The Fires of Heaven (Wheel of Time, #5) by Robert Jordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fires of Heaven</a>. It felt, to me, like a return to form, but all of this is pretty relative giv</span>
  <span id="freeText9612278914636215135" style="display:none"><i>Was the whole world really burning up?</i><br /><br />Thank goodness for the Wheel of Time <b>Wikia</b> page. At this point in the series I can’t really differentiate too clearly between books; everything is just blurring together. I suppose it would help if I read the books back to back, but that is not a realistic option. I honestly need a break between instalments. <br /><br />That said, I do believe I enjoyed this book more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13895.The_Fires_of_Heaven__Wheel_of_Time___5_" title="The Fires of Heaven (Wheel of Time, #5) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fires of Heaven</a>. It felt, to me, like a return to form, but all of this is pretty relative given my comment above. <br /><br />This time the story is actually moved forward. In fact, there are some pretty significant events that take place; let’s just say the deck is being shuffled. As per usual there is a <b>lot</b> of conniving, backstabbing and all kinds of political shenanigans between several factions, each of which with their own shady agenda. The Wheel of Time saga is a fantastic story but it is <b>stupendously</b> ambitious and intimidating. And, let’s be honest, more than a little bloated. Jordan’s vision, however, is singular in its scope and execution, and that is what pulls it through time and again. <br /><br /><i>Where are all the dead? <br />Why will they not be silent?</i><br /><br />As has been the trend so far, things are still getting darker and darker with each outing. It’s difficult to wrap my mind around the fact that this is only book six of fourteen. A <b>lot</b> has happened already and I’m not halfway yet. <br /><br /><i>No more running. <br />He would do what he had to do, but no more running.</i><br /><br /><u>Pros</u><br />1. The Dragon Reborn – this is the part of the story I enjoy the most. I love how everybody keeps underestimating Rand and his allies, and his sequences always have the most epic showdowns.<br />2. World building – say what you will about Robert Jordan but he know how to create a living, breathing, fully realised setting, complete with its own histories and legends, cultures and peoples, and whatever else you can think of.<br />3. Wolves!<br /><br /><u>Cons</u><br />1. Sexism, or whatever the hell this is – it seems to be a point of contention among readers, but it <b>is</b> detracting if (just about) every serious situation devolves into a pissing contest between men and women. <br />2. The sheer length of this book – if a book has a prologue of 72 pages it had better be paced pretty damned fast… <br /><br />The wolves. Let’s not forget the wolves…<br /><br /><i>Ground covered with brown grass, seemingly empty, suddenly gave birth to a thousand wolves.</i><br /><br />…which leads me to the Battle of Dumai’s Wells.<br /><br /><i>They will pay, [he] growled. I am the Lord of the Morning.</i><br /><br />See, here’s the clincher. It’s true that you could argue that this book has about 900 pages of build-up…. <b>BUT</b> it culminates in what is probably one of the most spectacular and satisfying showdowns in all of fantasy fiction. The <b>Battle of Dumai’s Wells</b> features almost 50,000 participants and just about blew my socks off, especially given the fact that it's over so quickly.<br /><br /><i>"Kneel and swear to the Lord Dragon, or you will be knelt."</i><br /><br />So, in summary: this is a long hard read, but it is ultimately rewarding. I am going with 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9612278914636215135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_313285569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313285569" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313285569?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313285569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3056487183580542052">This was another enjoyable instalment in the Wheel of Time series. It was an improvement on The Fires of Heaven, but did not reach the heights of The Shadow Rising( the best WoT book so far ). <br/><br/>It though Jordan did OK when it came to advancing the plot in this instalment. Not a ton happened, but it felt like a lot of stuff got set into motion. This meant a lot of focus on politics and scheming, but I've always been happy enough with such story arcs. <br/><br/>The characters proved a mixed bag: <br/><br/>Rand: I thou</span>
  <span id="freeText3056487183580542052" style="display:none">This was another enjoyable instalment in the Wheel of Time series. It was an improvement on The Fires of Heaven, but did not reach the heights of The Shadow Rising( the best WoT book so far ). <br /><br />It though Jordan did OK when it came to advancing the plot in this instalment. Not a ton happened, but it felt like a lot of stuff got set into motion. This meant a lot of focus on politics and scheming, but I've always been happy enough with such story arcs. <br /><br />The characters proved a mixed bag: <br /><br />Rand: I though the guy was the star of this instalment. I liked him a lot. He has really grown into the role of Dragon Reborn and does not baulk at the responsibilities or expectations. His dithering over his harem of women bounces between being amusing and annoying, but luckily was mostly amusing in this one.<br /><br />Perrin: I was happy he was back in the mix. Well, I was to start with. What is it with Rand's friends turning into asses the moment they get near him? We finally met Faile's family. They were as disturbing and crazy as you might expect given how she turned out.<br /><br />Mat: This was a good book for Mat. I still find him a bit whiny and annoying at times, but getting away from Rand and leading the Band of the Red Hand is helping him grow as a character. <br /><br />Egwene: Her best book so far. Like Mat she is beginning to show real maturity and positive growth. Her story arc was a little unbelievable and sudden, but it should be fun to see where it goes.<br /><br />Nynaeve: WTF has happened to the tough, brave, kick-ass Nynaeve of the first four books? She has totally morphed into a cringing, annoying, comedy character. And that is despite her still managing to do some pretty cool stuff! Jordan has totally ruined her character:(<br /><br />Elayne: Still stuck at the hip to Nynaeve, but she at least has fared better. <br /><br />Aviendha: She had a quiet book. At this stage she is little more than a romantic interest for Rand, and one that Jordan has on the back burner.<br /><br />Min: She had another good outing. I liked that she finally got to spend some time with Rand.<br /><br />The Aes Sedai: We got a whole batch of Aes Sedai POV's which I actually enjoyed. It definitely enhanced the story.<br /><br />The Forsaken: They are crazy and evil, but always fun to follow. It was great to meet the likes of Demondred and Semirhage in this one. Plus the introduction of the villainous Shadar Haroth was cool.<br /><br />All in all I found this to be an engaging and enjoyable read despite a few of the flaws I've just moaned about:)<br /><br />Rating: 4 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Another fantastic performance from Krammer and Reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3056487183580542052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1653896269">

<div id="review_337724808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337724808" />
    <a title="Christie Skipper Ritchotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte"><img alt="Christie Skipper Ritchotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308011651p2/1828577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337724808?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christie Skipper Ritchotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christie Skipper Ritchotte" href="/user/show/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte">Christie Skipper Ritchotte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte?shelf=failure-to-finish">failure-to-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte?shelf=needs-more-cowbell">needs-more-cowbell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1828577-christie-skipper-ritchotte?shelf=epic-in-scale">epic-in-scale</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337724808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16101012732033857144">On my future grave, I swear, the following is true. <br/><br/><br/>Once upon a time there was a book series called The Wheel of Time, which, when piled each volume upon the other, could reach past an elephant's rheumy eye. Once upon a time, after searching for a good new fantasy series, I began tWoT with a healthy gleam in my eye. What a blithe fool. What a tWoT.<br/><br/>I turned pulped wood pages by thousands, read a very-many lot-of words, until one day an annoying pattern manifested. Though I pressed on, it had beco</span>
  <span id="freeText16101012732033857144" style="display:none">On my future grave, I swear, the following is true. <br /><br /><br />Once upon a time there was a book series called The Wheel of Time, which, when piled each volume upon the other, could reach past an elephant's rheumy eye. Once upon a time, after searching for a good new fantasy series, I began tWoT with a healthy gleam in my eye. What a blithe fool. What a tWoT.<br /><br />I turned pulped wood pages by thousands, read a very-many lot-of words, until one day an annoying pattern manifested. Though I pressed on, it had become impossible to ignore the characters' skimpy appeal. The volume of unmanicured words kept drowning out the righteous words. Meandering plotlines had doubled back on each other, and I found they spelled out a mystic code to rival Davinci's own: Nyah, nyah, nyah-nyah, nyah. <br /><br />Dizzied and dismayed, I knew I had entered one of the circles of Hell, voluntarily; had been there months, perhaps even years. I peered woefully ahead to the four ponderous volumes (now seven) that waited with an infinite, mad patience, and realized my own hands had helped build this hell. I knew the only way to end the madness was to shot put Lord of Chaos across the room. <br /><br />With a vast effort and aching, calloused hands, I pushed the book away. The volume slammed the wall, leaving a great gash that flared alight and gaped like a page burning from the inside out. The gash in the wall became glass; a window (open!), revealing the glorious world beyond. <br /><br />I stumbled to the window, fell through the gap onto dewy, crisp grass. I walked into the reward of raucous birdsong and a biting wind that said, "You are alive." Alive! That day I left The Wheel of Time far behind me. <br /><br /><br />Last week, I found the stash of nine volumes in a dusty basement box. Years had passed, and still tWoT waited. Shakily, I taped the cardboard flaps, triple taped them. I placed a long-distance call to my younger brother, a fantasy novice, who had just finished reading The Lord of the Rings for the first time. "Have you been introduced to The Wheel of Time books?" I inquired. He hadn't been. Of course he hadn't. Whenever I start to feel guilty, I remind myself: I didn't like my brother much anyway. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16101012732033857144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
